codex
The patch introduces a security issue in the new join-token flow, weakens the intended enforcement of the mandatory review gate, and breaks persistence of the renamed customer-memory occasion. These are discrete regressions that should be addressed before considering the change correct.

Full review comments:

- [P1] Bind the join token to the intended destination account — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\functions\src\join_decision_circle.ts:124-165
  When `includeJoinLink` is used, the HMAC payload only proves `{shopId, projectId, originalCustomerUid}` and the callable then accepts **any** authenticated caller whose `uid == destUid`. In practice, if the WhatsApp link is forwarded or opened on the wrong device by another signed-in customer of the same shop, they can supply their own `destUid` and `joinDecisionCircle` will reassign that project's `customerUid` and chat participants to them. This new bearer-token flow needs to bind the token to the intended recipient (or otherwise confirm `destUid`) before moving ownership.

- [P2] Make the review marker freshness check cover the latest PR commit — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\.github\workflows\codex-review-gate.yml:64-79
  The current anti-staleness check only verifies that `.codex-review-passed` was modified somewhere between `BASE_SHA` and `HEAD_SHA`. That still passes if a contributor runs `codex review`, commits the marker, and then adds more code afterward without rerunning review, so the gate can approve a PR whose final diff was never reviewed. If this workflow is meant to be blocking, freshness needs to be tied to the tip commit (or at least to all commits after the marker update).

- [P2] Preserve round-trip serialization for `betiKaGhar` occasions — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\packages\lib_core\lib\src\models\customer_memory.dart:27-29
  Renaming the enum case but pinning its JSON value to `'dahej'` breaks the existing `CustomerMemoryRepo.upsertMemory()` write path, which serializes occasions with `e.name`. After this change, selecting `PreferredOccasion.betiKaGhar` writes `'betiKaGhar'`, but `CustomerMemory.fromJson()` only recognizes `'dahej'` for that enum member, so the next read will deserialize the saved value as `other`. Any newly edited customer-memory record using this option will therefore come back corrupted.
The patch introduces a security issue in the new join-token flow, weakens the intended enforcement of the mandatory review gate, and breaks persistence of the renamed customer-memory occasion. These are discrete regressions that should be addressed before considering the change correct.

Full review comments:

- [P1] Bind the join token to the intended destination account — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\functions\src\join_decision_circle.ts:124-165
  When `includeJoinLink` is used, the HMAC payload only proves `{shopId, projectId, originalCustomerUid}` and the callable then accepts **any** authenticated caller whose `uid == destUid`. In practice, if the WhatsApp link is forwarded or opened on the wrong device by another signed-in customer of the same shop, they can supply their own `destUid` and `joinDecisionCircle` will reassign that project's `customerUid` and chat participants to them. This new bearer-token flow needs to bind the token to the intended recipient (or otherwise confirm `destUid`) before moving ownership.

- [P2] Make the review marker freshness check cover the latest PR commit — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\.github\workflows\codex-review-gate.yml:64-79
  The current anti-staleness check only verifies that `.codex-review-passed` was modified somewhere between `BASE_SHA` and `HEAD_SHA`. That still passes if a contributor runs `codex review`, commits the marker, and then adds more code afterward without rerunning review, so the gate can approve a PR whose final diff was never reviewed. If this workflow is meant to be blocking, freshness needs to be tied to the tip commit (or at least to all commits after the marker update).

- [P2] Preserve round-trip serialization for `betiKaGhar` occasions — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\packages\lib_core\lib\src\models\customer_memory.dart:27-29
  Renaming the enum case but pinning its JSON value to `'dahej'` breaks the existing `CustomerMemoryRepo.upsertMemory()` write path, which serializes occasions with `e.name`. After this change, selecting `PreferredOccasion.betiKaGhar` writes `'betiKaGhar'`, but `CustomerMemory.fromJson()` only recognizes `'dahej'` for that enum member, so the next read will deserialize the saved value as `other`. Any newly edited customer-memory record using this option will therefore come back corrupted.
